# Findings Register — full disposition of every note across the validation campaign

> ⚠️ **FULL RE-VALIDATION RESET — 2026-06-24.** All units have been reset to **⬜ pending** in [VALIDATION_LEDGER.md](VALIDATION_LEDGER.md) and `docs/checklists/` for a fresh end-to-end re-verification (extensive code changes during the limitations-elimination campaign). The dispositions below are **retained as historical evidence** but are **SUPERSEDED** until each unit is re-validated.

**Date:** 2026-06-12   **Library:** Seqeron.Genomics (mission-critical)
**Source:** every note/limitation/follow-up across all 86 reports in `docs/Validation/reports/`.

Each finding is placed in exactly one category:

| Category | Meaning |
|----------|---------|
| **FIXED-NOW** | Non-radical (doc/comment/spec text or small safe code change). Fixed in this pass. |
| **FEASIBLE → IMPLEMENT** | Needs real code change but is implementable safely with strict tests, in its own context. |
| **NOT-POSSIBLE (radical)** | Requires a redesign / public-API change / new model. Documented here, not changed. |
| **BY-DESIGN** | Note documents *correct, sourced* intended behaviour; "fixing" it would be wrong. No change. |

---

| A-MIRNA-CLEAVAGE-001-1 | MIRNA-CLEAVAGE-001 (re-validation) | **Doc-comment overstatement + test-quality (no algorithm defect).** `PredictDroshaDicerCleavage` faithfully realises the Han 2006 +11-bp Drosha ruler and the Park 2011 22-nt 5'-counting Dicer rule — the 5p mature reproduces miRBase hsa-miR-21-5p (MIMAT0000076) `UAGCUUAUCAGACUGAUGUUGA` EXACTLY (real precursor MI0000077, 11-nt lower stem reconstructed, junction 0 → +11). But the XML doc-comment on `DroshaCut3Prime`/`StarStart` claimed the 3p (miRNA*) span is "the base on the 3' arm cut by Drosha"; the code actually places it 2 nt 3' of the 5p mature end in LINEAR coordinates (no hairpin folding), so the predicted star (`GCUUAUCAGACUGAUGUUGACU`) is NOT the real 3' arm hsa-miR-21-3p (`CAACACCAGUCGAUGGGCUGU`, MIMAT0004494). Recovering the true 3p arm needs folding (out of scope, like the trained miRDeep2 classifier). Test DD5 was a code echo (`StarSequence == pri.Substring(13,22)`). | Corrected the record doc-comment + added a `<remarks>` scope/limitation paragraph + fixed the inline body comment to state the linear-geometry approximation (no behaviour change). Replaced the DD5 code-echo with rule-derived coordinates + order-robust invariant; added DD11 (real MI0000077 precursor: 5p reproduced, linear star ≠ real 3p), DD12 (no-stem still returns ruler coords), DD13 (non-ACGU passed through), DD14 (length boundary 35/34). Full `dotnet test Seqeron.sln` green (Genomics 18775 passed, Failed: 0). State: CLEAN. |
| A14 | SV-DETECT-001 (Phase-2) | **Real algorithm defect.** `IsConcordantOrientation` treated RF (reverse-forward, outward-facing / "everted") pairs as concordant, so an RF pair was never flagged discordant; `ClassifySV` had no Duplication branch. Per DELLY (Rausch et al. 2012), LUMPY, Manta and SVXplorer (Kumar et al. 2020) — and the unit's own cureffi/BWA source ("RF, FF or RR … that's a problem") — RF is the basic **tandem-duplication** signature for a short-insert FR library, hence discordant; only FR is the proper-pair (FLAG 0x02) orientation. Test S4 was green-washed (asserted RF "not discordant"). Description (SV_Detection.md), Evidence and TestSpec all repeated the wrong "FR/RF both concordant" claim. | Fixed `IsConcordantOrientation` → FR only; added RF→`SVType.Duplication` branch to `ClassifySV`; rewrote S4 to assert RF discordant→Duplication; added M9 ClassifySV Duplication test; corrected the description/Evidence/TestSpec and added DELLY + SVXplorer refs. Full suite 6485 green. |
| A16 | ANNOT-CODING-001 (Phase-2) | **Real algorithm defect.** `CalculateCodingPotential` (CPAT hexamer usage-bias `kmer_ratio`, frame 0) handled the both-zero in-both hexamer wrongly: it fell through and unconditionally incremented the scored-hexamer count, treating a `coding==0 && noncoding==0` hexamer as a counted contribution of 0. The canonical CPAT reference (`liguowang/cpat` `src/cpmodule/FrameKmer.py` lines 95-96) and the lncScore copy (`WGLab/lncScore` `tools/cpmodule/FrameKmer.py` lines 90-91) — both fetched this session — have `elif coding[k]==0 and noncoding[k]==0: continue`, so the hexamer is **skipped and NOT counted** (`frame0_count` not incremented). Counting it inflates the denominator and dilutes the mean. Test C1 was a code-echo: it asserted the wrong "counted as 0, halves the next contribution" value (0.6931471805599453). Evidence `kmer_ratio` transcription, TestSpec C1, and algorithm doc §2.2/§5.2/§6.1 all omitted the both-zero `continue` branch. | Added `else if (coding==0 && noncoding==0) continue;` plus a trailing `else continue;` before `scoredHexamers++` (verbatim to canonical `kmer_ratio`); rewrote C1 → `CalculateCodingPotential_BothTablesZero_HexamerIsSkipped` asserting the sourced 1.3862943611198906 (only AAACCC counted); corrected Evidence code block + corner cases, TestSpec C1 row + coverage table, and the algorithm doc. Full unfiltered suite 6561 green; build 0 errors. |
| A18 | SEQ-GC-ANALYSIS-001 (Phase-2) | Test-quality only (**no algorithm defect**). `AnalyzeGcContent` realises every sourced formula exactly — GC% = (G+C)/(A+T+G+C)×100 (Wikipedia GC-content/Brock), GC skew & AT skew = (G−C)/(G+C), (A−T)/(A+T) with zero-division→0 (Wikipedia GC skew; Biopython `GC_skew`; Charneski et al. 2011), and population variance Σ(x−μ)²/N (Cuemath, anchor {12,13,12,14,19}=6.8) — all four sources fetched live this session; hand-verified every fixture value. Two coverage gaps: the documented **lower skew bound** "pure-C → −1" (Wikipedia "−1 ⇔ G=0") was only exercised indirectly inside M4's variance, never asserted directly; and **AT skew was only tested at 0** (M3, M9), so a sign-flip `(T−A)/(A+T)` or wrong-denominator `(A−T)/n` would have passed. | Added `AnalyzeGcContent_PureCytosine_SkewIsMinusOneContentIsHundred` (`CCCC`→ skew −1, GC% 100) and `AnalyzeGcContent_AdenineRich_AtSkewIsPositiveHalf` (`AAAT` A3T1 → (3−1)/(3+1)=+0.5), both exact-sourced. Fixture 13→15; full unfiltered suite 6609 green; build 0 errors. |
| A17 | ANNOT-REPEAT-001 (Phase-2) | **Real algorithm defect.** `ClassifyRepeat` matched a library element by *bidirectional* substring containment (`query.Contains(element) || element.Contains(query)`). The reverse direction (`element.Contains(query)`) let a trivially short query inherit a class purely because a longer consensus happens to contain those letters — e.g. a single base `"A"` was classified `SINE/Alu` because the 20-bp Alu consensus contains an `A`, and any 1-bp query matches almost any library. This contradicts RepeatMasker's model (Smit/Hubley/Green; webrepeatmaskerhelp.html), which **screens the query for occurrences of known library elements** and reports the best match found *within* the query — not the query being a fragment of a consensus. No MUST test depended on the reverse direction; the existing tests never exercised a short/sub-consensus query, so the defect was uncaught (would also have passed against the wrong impl). | Made matching one-directional (`element ⊆ query`) and updated the XML doc; corrected Evidence Assumption 1 + TestSpec Assumption 1 (drop "either direction / is contained by"). Added M7b (single base `"A"`→`Unknown`), M7c (`GGCCGGG` fragment of Alu consensus→`Unknown`), M5b (longest-match wins when several elements occur→`SINE/Alu`), M6b (empty→`Simple_repeat`), and INV-3 reverse-complement arm test (revcomp(GAA)=TTC, revcomp(TTACG)=CGTAA, revcomp(GGATCC)=GGATCC). Full unfiltered suite 6566 green; build 0 errors. |
| A18 | GENOMIC-REPEAT-001 (Phase-2) | **Real algorithm defect.** `FindRepeats` emitted only the *full* longest-common-prefix of each adjacent pair of sorted suffixes, not its shorter prefixes. A substring occurs ≥ 2 times iff it is a *prefix* of some adjacent-pair LCP (standard LCP-array result), so emitting only the maximal LCP drops every shorter repeated prefix that is not itself a maximal LCP elsewhere — violating the documented contract (Repeat_Detection.md §1: "enumerates **every** distinct substring occurring at least twice with length ≥ minimum"). Verified against the built assembly: `FindRepeats("ACGTACGTTTTTACGT", 3)` returned 5 substrings `{ACGT, CGT, TACGT, TTT, TTTT}` but the brute-force ground truth (every `s[i:j]` length ≥ 3 occurring ≥ 2 times, cross-checked vs the sorted-suffix LCP set) is 8: it also includes `ACG@{0,4,12}`, `TAC@{3,11}`, `TACG@{3,11}`. The TestSpec/Evidence M6 row asserted the buggy 5-item set — a code echo that passes against the defective code and fails the sourced definition. `FindLongestRepeat` is unaffected and correct (LRS values match Wikipedia/GeeksforGeeks + brute force). | Replaced the single-LCP emission with a loop over every prefix length `max(1,minLength)..lcpLen` (dedup via HashSet, positions via `FindAllOccurrences`); updated the XML doc + Repeat_Detection.md §4.1/§5.2/§7. Corrected M6 to the sourced 8-item set with exact positions and added **M8** (`FindRepeats("ACGTACGT", 2)` → exact 6-item set) as a completeness regression guard that fails against the old impl. Updated Evidence + TestSpec M6/M8 to brute-force ground truth. Full unfiltered suite 6571 green; build 0 errors. |
| A19 | RNA-PAIR-001 (Phase-2) | Test-quality only (no algorithm defect): `GetComplement` IUPAC degenerate test S3 exercised only N, R, Y, leaving the *sourced* complement branches S, W, K, M, B, D, H, V (and lowercase-degenerate + non-IUPAC pass-through) unasserted — real source-defined logic with no test (would also pass against a wrong impl on those arms). Algorithm itself matches all retrieved sources exactly: pair set {GC,CG,AU,UA (WatsonCrick), GU,UG (Wobble)} confirmed independently by **ViennaRNA RNAlib** default `md.pair` allowed-pair set and by Crick 1966 + Wikipedia Base pair/Wobble; complement table matches IUPAC-IUB (1970) full table (W↔W, S↔S, M↔K, R↔Y, B↔V, D↔H, N↔N) and Biopython `complement_rna("CGAUT")="GCUAA"`. | Strengthened S3 to assert all 11 degenerate complements with exact IUPAC values; added `GetComplement_LowercaseIupacDegenerate_ReturnsExpected` (r→Y, n→N, k→M) and `GetComplement_NonIupacChar_PassesThroughUnchanged` ('-'→'-', 'X'→'X'). | A20 | ONCO-CNA-003 (Phase-2) | **Test-coverage gap only (no algorithm defect).** `DetectHomozygousDeletions`/`IsHomozygousDeletion`/`IdentifyDeletedTumorSuppressors` realise the validated model verbatim, re-verified this session against **WebFetched** sources: Cheng et al. 2017 PMC5663922 (homozygous deletion = "regions having zero copies of both alleles" = total CN 0; distinct from hemizygous single-copy loss), cBioPortal FAQ (−2 Deep Deletion = possibly homozygous; −1 Shallow = heterozygous, NOT homozygous; 0/1/2 not deletions — all verbatim), the **CNVkit `cnvlib/call.py` `absolute_threshold` source** (`if row.log2 <= thresh:` inclusive `<=`, count up from 0, `np.ceil` above last, NaN→neutral CN), and NCBI Gene cytobands (TP53 17p13.1, RB1 13q14.2, CDKN2A 9p21.3, PTEN 10q23.31, BRCA1 17q21.31, BRCA2 13q13.1 — arm panel + 13q→{RB1,BRCA2} confirmed). Hand-traced CN table (−1.1 boundary→CN0, −1.0999→CN1, NaN→neutral, custom −0.4 cutoff→CN0) matches code and tests. The 22-test fixture asserted exact sourced values (no green-washing) but left 5 **documented** behaviours untested. **Stage-A NOTE (non-blocking):** repo `DefaultCopyNumberThresholds` = (−1.1,−0.25,0.2,0.7) vs published CNVkit `call` default (−1.1,−0.4,0.3,0.7) — only the deletion cutoff governs CN 0 and **−1.1 is identical**, so no homozygous-deletion result is affected; this is an ONCO-CNA-001 concern, not this unit's. | Added 5 tests for documented-but-untested behaviour (exact contract/sourced values, no echoes): `DetectHomozygousDeletions_NonPositiveArmLength_Throws` (TestSpec C3 "ArmLength ≤ 0" arm, previously only End≤Start tested), `DetectHomozygousDeletions_NonPositivePloidy_Throws` (ArgumentOutOfRangeException), `DetectHomozygousDeletions_InvalidThresholds_Throws` (non-ascending + wrong-count → ArgumentException), `IsHomozygousDeletion_DeletionCutoffBoundary_TrueThenFalse` (−1.1 true / −1.0999 false), `IsHomozygousDeletion_InvalidSegment_Throws`. No assertion weakened, no skip, no tolerance widened. Fixture 22→28; full unfiltered suite **6660 green**; build 0 errors. |
| A15 | TRANS-SPLICE-001 (Phase-2) | **Real algorithm defect.** `DetectAlternativeSplicing` swapped the A5SS/A3SS labels: two alternative exons sharing their START but differing in END were classified `AlternativeThreePrimeSS`, and sharing their END but differing in START as `AlternativeFivePrimeSS` — the reverse of the standard convention. On the + strand the 5′ splice site = donor = the 3′ END of the upstream exon and the 3′ splice site = acceptor = the 5′ START of the downstream exon, so shared-start/different-end is an alternative **donor** = **A5SS** and shared-end/different-start is an alternative **acceptor** = **A3SS** (verified vs Xinglab/rmats-turbo README A5SS/A3SS coordinate columns — A5SS forms differ at the downstream/END boundary, A3SS at the upstream/START boundary; corroborated by NAR 34(21):6305 and the molecular-biology donor/acceptor definitions). Tests M8/M9, the TestSpec rows and the Evidence dataset all encoded the same swapped labels (code-echoes that would pass against the wrong code). | Swapped the two branch labels in `ClassifyIsoformPair`; corrected M8/M9 test names + assertions to the sourced types and added Start/End span assertions; corrected the TestSpec M8/M9 rows + §5.6 table and the Evidence dataset table; added the rMATS coordinate-convention evidence point. No other caller depends on the labels. Full suite 6501 green. |

| A17 | CODON-RSCU-001 (Phase-2) | **Test-coverage gap only (no algorithm defect).** `CalculateRscu`/`CountCodons` realise the canonical RSCU family-ratio formula `RSCU_{i,j}=(n_i·x_{i,j})/Σx` verified verbatim this session against the **fetched** LIRMM "RSCU RS" page (`RSCU_{i,j}=(n_i×x_{i,j})/Σ x_{i,j}`, no-bias=1) and GenomicSig (CRAN) (bounds `[0,n_i]`, observed/expected-under-uniform), corroborated by seqinr `uco` (Sharp/Tuohy/Mosurski 1986 primary ref). All values independently hand-computed and confirmed by the code: Leu `CTGCTGCTGCTA` 4.5/1.5/0 (Σ=6); Phe `TTTTTTTTC` 4/3,2/3; equal `TTTTTC` 1.0/1.0; Met `ATGATG` 1.0; absent family `ATGATG`→0; stop family `TAATAGTGA` 1.0 each; biased stop `TAATAATGA` 2.0/1.0/0.0 (Σ=3). The original 16-test fixture covered all formula paths/invariants/CountCodons/guards but left two **documented** Stage-A branches untested. | Added three exact-value tests (independently sourced, not code echoes): `CalculateRscu_AbsentFamily_ReturnsZeroForEveryCodon` (locks Assumption #1: 0/0 family→0, no pseudocount); `CalculateRscu_StopCodonFamily_TreatedAsThreeFoldFamily` and `CalculateRscu_StopFamilyBiased_ComputesFamilyRatioAndSumsToDegeneracy` (lock Assumption #2: TAA/TAG/TGA as a 3-fold family via the same family-ratio formula). No assertion weakened, no skip, no tolerance widened. Fixture 16→19 tests. Full unfiltered suite 6526 green, build 0 errors. |
| A18 | CODON-ENC-001 (Phase-2) | **Test code-echo defect + documented edge-case divergence (no defect on real input).** The original M3 (29.0) and M5 (40.4) expected values were echoes of an **unsourced** fallback: when an entire 2/4/6-fold degeneracy class is absent, the code (`ClassContribution`) adds the class's *full codon count* (e.g. +9). The de-facto reference **codonW** (Peden thesis, fetched + `pdftotext` this session) states the opposite: "For sequences where a synonymous family of amino-acids is empty (F̂ₙ=0), **Nc is not calculated**", with only the isoleucine 3-fold exception (Eq. 5a). Those tests would pass against the very behaviour the spec itself listed as failure-mode #2. The **core formula** (Wright Eq. 1/3/4/5a + cap-61, Fuglsang 2004) is correct — verified exact to double precision against an independent Python reference (fully-populated biased gene 41.288461538461526; Ile-absent Eq.5a-active 39.47394540942927; 2:1-bias 56.0; one-codon-per-aa 20.0). The whole-class-absent path is unreachable on real coding sequences. | Rewrote M3→fully-populated biased gene (exact 41.288461538461526) and M5→all-classes-but-Ile so Eq.5a genuinely fires (exact 39.47394540942927), both traced to the independent reference (not code echoes); added M5b pinning the whole-class-absent value (29.0) explicitly labelled LIBRARY-SPECIFIC / NOT-Wright in name+comment+message so it cannot be mistaken for sourced. Updated TestSpec §4.1/§7 to record the codonW divergence honestly. No assertion weakened, no skip, no tolerance widened (lower clamp at 20 left as documented defensive bound). A full contract fix (return NaN/sentinel for "Nc undefined") would ripple into `GetStatistics` + MCP `EncResult` — logged as optional FR, out of scope for one session. Full unfiltered suite 6527 green, build 0 errors. |

| A20 | ASSEMBLY-COVER-001 (Phase-2) | **Test-coverage gap only (no algorithm defect).** `SequenceAssembler.CalculateCoverage` realises per-base depth (depth[i]=#placed reads spanning i) exactly. Formulas confirmed verbatim this session against the **fetched** Cook page (depth=`Sum of Depths / genome size`, breadth=`Bases Mapped / genome size`), Metagenomics Wiki (breadth 32876/45678=0.719) and Illumina (Lander-Waterman `C = LN/G`). Worked M1 (`ACGTTGCAAT` + `ACGTT`/`TTGCA`/`GCAAT`) hand-traced through `FindBestAlignment` → [1,1,1,2,2,2,2,2,1,1], Σ=15, avg 1.5, breadth 1.0; cross-checked by C=LN/G = 5·3/10 = 1.5 (two independent methods agree). PASS-WITH-NOTES on Stage A: the sources' "read overhanging the reference end contributes its overlapping portion" convention is **unreachable** here — `FindBestAlignment` only places a read where it fits entirely (scan `0…refLen−readLen`), so the `min(p+L,refLen)` clip is dead/defensive code and an over-long read just fails to place (M4 all-zero). Verified this session against the **fetched** cutadapt `quality_trim_index` (qualtrim.pyx: two independent full-read passes, each `if s<0: break`, then `if start>=stop: start,stop=0,0`) and BWA `bwa_trim_read` (`if (s < 0) break;`). The missing early break is exactly the documented refinement that "allows some good-quality bases among the bad ones": a high-quality base near an end should protect the interior from that end's pass. A randomized comparison of the old code vs the cutadapt reference diverged on **~19.5%** of reads (38,989/200,000). Minimal repro: qualities 20,0,8,40 (`5!)I`), cutoff 10 — cutadapt keeps all 4 bases; old code kept only the last. **Every pre-existing test (M1–M5,S1–S3) was a happy-path case that agreed with cutadapt**, so the suite shared the code's blind spot. | Added the `s<0` early break to both `TrimEnd`/`TrimStart` (sign-flipped `if (sum > 0) break;`); both passes now run independently over the full read; added the `start>=stop ⇒ (0,0)` drop rule. Verified the fixed algorithm against cutadapt `quality_trim_index` over **300,000 random reads × 3 cutoffs (1,10,20): 0 mismatches**. Added 3 exact-value tests that fail against the old code and trace to cutadapt: `GoodBaseAt3PrimeEnd_KeepsLowQualityInterior` (`5!)I`→`ACGT`), `IsolatedGoodBaseInBadRead_KeepsOnlyGoodBase` (`##I##`→`G`), `WindowsCross_DropsRead` (`5&&`→dropped). Corrected the description (`Quality_Trimming.md` §4.1/§5.2/§5.3/§2.5/Deviations) to document the early break and the `start>=stop` rule. No assertion weakened, no skip. Fixture 11→14 tests. ## B. FEASIBLE → IMPLEMENT (own context, strict tests first, project patterns)

| # | Unit | Finding | Planned implementation |
|---|------|---------|------------------------|
| B1 | PROTMOTIF-PROSITE-001 | Extended ScanProsite `*` (Kleene-star) query metachar silently dropped → a pattern using it is silently mis-parsed. | **Reject** unsupported PROSITE metacharacters with a clear exception (mirror the Newick "throw, don't silently drop" fix). Strict tests. |
| B2 | POP-FST-001 | `CalculateFst` silently truncates to `min(count1,count2)` on mismatched locus counts. | Validate equal locus counts → throw `ArgumentException` on mismatch (defensive contract). Strict tests. |
| B3 | PARSE-EMBL-001 | INSDC doubled-quote escaping `""`→`"` not unescaped in qualifier values; plus a dead `QualifierRegex` path. | Unescape `""`→`"` in qualifier parsing; remove dead code. Strict tests with the doubled-quote case. |
| B4 | SPLICE-PREDICT-001 (LIMITED) | Region shorter than `minExonLength` dropped by `DeriveExons` but kept by `GenerateSplicedSequence` → coverage/spliced-length invariants (INV-3/4/11) inconsistent. | Make the two consistent (spliced sequence derives from the same reported-exon set), restoring all invariants while preserving `minExonLength` semantics and the `start<end` property test. Strict tests. |
| B5 | RNA-PARTITION-001 | `CalculatePartitionFunction` computed `BasePairProbabilities` with the **external decomposition only** (`Q(0,i-1)·Q^b·Q(j+1,n)/Z`). Wrong for any pair that can be **nested** inside another pair — those are under-reported (e.g. `GGGAAACCC` E_bp=0: P[2,6] returned 0.05, true 0.30; `GGGGCCCC` P[1,5] returned 0.0625, true 0.1875). The Z value was correct; only the probabilities were wrong. Tests M5/M6 were blind to it: they only checked outermost (never-enclosed) pairs. The Evidence + algorithm docs repeated the same false "external suffices in the flat model" claim (Stage-A defect). | Replace with the full McCaskill **outside recursion** `P[i,j]=Q^b(i,j)·O(i,j)/Z`, `O(i,j)=Q(0,i-1)·Q(j+1,n-1)+Σ_{k<i,l>j} w·Q(k+1,i-1)·Q(j+1,l-1)·O(k,l)`, pairs processed outermost-first. Verified vs exhaustive (weighted) brute force to 3.3e-16 on `GGGGCCCC`/`GGGAAACCC` and 300 random seqs; per-base ≤1 invariant holds. Add strict per-pair tests for nested pairs (E_bp=0 and −1) + per-base ≤1 test; fix Evidence/algorithm docs. **✅ DONE this session.** |

## C. NOT-POSSIBLE (radical — documented, not changed in this pass)

| # | Unit | Gap | Why radical / what a real fix needs |
|---|------|-----|--------------------------------------|
| C1 | META-CLASS-001 | True taxonomic classification (Kraken weighted root-to-leaf / LCA). | ✅ **IMPLEMENTED** (approved breaking API change). Replaced the flat best-hit classifier with a faithful Kraken classifier (Wood & Salzberg 2014, Genome Biology 15:R46, **WebFetched** this session via PMC4053813). **New public surface:** (1) `TaxonomyTree` (+ `TaxonNode(Id,Name,Rank,ParentId)` record) — an NCBI-style taxonomy with `GetPathToRoot`, `IsAncestorOf`, `GetDepth`, and `Lca(a,b)`/`Lca(IEnumerable<int>)` (pairwise-fold) lowest-common-ancestor; (2) `BuildKmerDatabase(IEnumerable<(int TaxonId,string Sequence)>, TaxonomyTree, k=31) → Dictionary<string,int>` mapping each canonical k-mer to the **LCA of all taxa whose references contain it** ("if a k-mer … has had its LCA value previously set, then the LCA of the stored value and the current sequence's taxon is calculated"); (3) `ClassifyReads(reads, IReadOnlyDictionary<string,int>, TaxonomyTree, k=31)` returning the **RTL** assignment — hit taxa + ancestors form the classification tree, each node weighted by its k-mer count, the **maximum-scoring root-to-leaf path** is chosen and its leaf assigned, **ties broken by the LCA of the maximally-scoring leaves**; no-hit reads → root/unclassified (`TaxonomyTree.RootId`). `TaxonomicClassification` redesigned to `(ReadId, TaxonId, TaxonName, Rank, RtlScore, Confidence=C/Q, MatchedKmers=C, TotalKmers=Q, Kingdom…Species lineage)`. **Removed/broken:** the old `BuildKmerDatabase(IEnumerable<(string,string)>, int) → Dictionary<string,string>` and `ClassifyReads(reads, IReadOnlyDictionary<string,string>, int)` and the string-taxonomy `TaxonomicClassification` shape. **Other call sites updated:** MCP `MetagenomicsTools.ClassifyReads`/`BuildKmerDatabase` (new `int` taxon ids + `TaxonNodeInput[]` taxonomy + `AppJsonContext` registration), the metagenomics snapshot tests. **Tests rewritten:** the 27 locked META-CLASS tests replaced by a 26-test suite on a hand-built taxonomy (root→Archaea / root→Bacteria→Proteobacteria→Gammaproteobacteria→Enterobacteriaceae→{Escherichia→{E.coli, E.fergusonii}, Salmonella→S.enterica}) with hand-derived expectations: LCA unit tests (siblings 100,101→genus 20; ancestor/descendant 20,100→20; self 100→100; disjoint 5,100→root 1; cross-genus 100,200→family 10); DB-build LCA collapse (shared k-mer `AGCT`→Lca(100,101)=20); single-species read→100; equal split within genus→genus 20 (LCA of tied leaves); equal split across genera→family 10; RTL ancestor-weight single winner (100×1,101×2,genus20×1 → RTL(101)=3>RTL(100)=2 → 101, C=2,Q=4); no-hit/empty/ambiguous→root; RC canonical lookup. **Mutation-checked:** reverting DB-build to first-wins and the tie-break to first-leaf fails 3 tests. Full unfiltered suite **6760 green**; build 0 errors. (The pre-existing net9.0 MCP project is unbuildable with the in-env net8 SDK regardless of this change; its source was updated to the new signatures.) |
| C2 | Phylogenetics (PHYLO-NEWICK / TREE / COMP) | Full N-ary (multifurcating) trees. | ✅ **IMPLEMENTED** (approved breaking API change). Refactored `PhyloNode` from the binary `Left`/`Right` model to **N-ary (multifurcating)**: the canonical storage is now `List<PhyloNode> Children` (0 = leaf, 2 = bifurcation, ≥3 = polytomy/multifurcation); `Left`/`Right` are retained as convenience accessors over `Children[0]`/`Children[1]` so binary-tree call sites and tests are source-compatible. **Sourced rules (this session):** (1) **Newick multifurcation** — grammar `BranchSet → Branch ("," Branch)*`; "a node is multifurcating if it has three or more immediate descendant lineages" (WebSearch, Wikipedia "Newick format"). The PHYLO-NEWICK throw-on->2-children guard is **removed**: `ParseNewick`/`ToNewick` now parse and write genuine polytomies `(A,B,C);`. (2) **NJ trifurcation** — Neighbor-Joining infers an *unrooted* tree; the loop now stops at three OTUs and connects them at one central node (the characteristic trifurcation), branch lengths from the additive 3-taxon system `L_i=(d_ij+d_ik−d_jk)/2` (Saitou & Nei 1987; WebSearch). (3) **RF with multifurcations** — RF = symmetric difference of non-trivial split/clade sets; contracting an internal edge (a multifurcation) simply removes that split from Σ(T), so an unresolved node contributes fewer bipartitions/clades (WebSearch; Briand et al. 2020 generalized RF — refinement/contraction are inverses). **Consumers updated** to traverse `Children`: UPGMA (verified still strictly bifurcating), NJ (trifurcating centre), `ToNewick`/`ParseNewick`, rooted-clade RF + unrooted-bipartition `CalculateUnrootedRobinsonFoulds`, MRCA, `GetLeaves`/`CalculateTreeLength`/`GetTreeDepth`, `PatristicDistance`, bootstrap. MCP `Seqeron.Mcp.Phylogenetics` uses only the stable public method API (no direct `Left`/`Right` access) so it needs no source change (net9, unbuildable on the in-env net8 SDK regardless). **Tests rewritten/added (hand-derived):** the two ParseNewick "throws-on-multifurcation" tests replaced by 4 N-ary Newick tests (`(A,B,C);`→3-child node + identical round-trip; nested `(A,B,(C,D,E));`; branch-length preservation `(A:0.1,B:0.2,C:0.3);`→`(A:0.1000,B:0.2000,C:0.3000);`); NJ trifurcation round-trip on the Wikipedia 5-taxon matrix (`(((a,b),c),d,e)`, 3-child root, byte-for-byte Newick round-trip; additive correctness covered by the pre-existing patristic-distance test, verified independently in Python); the NJ bootstrap test corrected to the trifurcating-root reality (`((A,B),C,D)` → single clade `{A,B}`, `{C,D}` no longer a rooted clade); RF-collapse tests (binary `(((A,B),C),(D,E))` vs collapsed `((A,B,C),(D,E))` → rooted RF **1** and unrooted RF **1** = the one resolved split lost — hand-derived); MRCA over a 3-child polytomy; tree-stats (length 2.1, depth 2, patristic A→C across the polytomy) over a polytomy; UPGMA-stays-binary (every internal node exactly 2 children). **Mutation-checked:** RF-of-tree-with-itself = 0 guards the RF-collapse value; the patristic A→C polytomy assertion fails a binary-only (first-two-children) traversal. Full unfiltered suite **6768 green**; build 0 errors. |
| C3 | PHYLO-COMP-001 | Unrooted-bipartition Robinson-Foulds as an alternative to the current rooted-clade metric. | ✅ **IMPLEMENTED** (additive, non-breaking). Added `PhylogeneticAnalyzer.CalculateUnrootedRobinsonFoulds(t1,t2)` (symmetric difference of the sets of non-trivial leaf **bipartitions**/splits — the original Robinson & Foulds 1981 metric; `RF = \|A\B\| + \|B\A\|`; trivial leaf-edge splits excluded; binary `PhyloNode` read as unrooted by canonicalising each split to its smaller {S, complement} side) plus `CalculateNormalizedUnrootedRobinsonFoulds` (`RF / (2n−6)`). The existing rooted-clade `RobinsonFouldsDistance` is byte-for-byte unchanged. Sources retrieved this session: Robinson & Foulds (1981); Wikipedia "Robinson–Foulds metric" (RF = A+B over partitions, divide-by/normalize variants); Rice comp571 tree-metrics **worked example** (T1 {BC\|ADE, ABC\|DE} vs T2 {AB\|CDE, ABC\|DE} → one differing internal split each → **RF = 2**). 10 strict tests (URF-M01..M04, URF-ROOT, URF-N01/N02, URF-E01..E03): identical→0; single NNI→2; **root-invariance** — `((A,B),(C,(D,E)))` vs `(((A,B),C),(D,E))` (same unrooted tree, different root) → unrooted RF **0** while rooted-clade RF **2**; max 5-taxon→2(n−3)=4; normalized 0/0.5/1 and n=3→denominator 0→0; <3 leaves / mismatched leaf sets / null → throw. **Mutation-checked:** replacing the bipartition set with rooted clades fails 5 tests incl. URF-ROOT (a rooted-clade impl of the new method is detected). Full unfiltered suite **6711 green**; build 0 errors. |
| C4 | ALIGN-MULTI-001 | Guide-tree progressive MSA. | ✅ **IMPLEMENTED** (additive, non-breaking). Added `SequenceAligner.MultipleAlignProgressive(IEnumerable<DnaSequence>, ScoringMatrix?)` — the Feng-Doolittle / Clustal-style progressive method — alongside the existing star `MultipleAlign`, which is byte-for-byte unchanged (verified: star still returns its length-6 gapped result on the discriminating input). Pipeline: (1) all C(k,2) pairwise **Needleman-Wunsch** alignments (reuses `GlobalAlignCore`) → distance matrix with distance = 1 − fractional identity (identical columns / pairwise alignment length); (2) **UPGMA** guide tree over that matrix (proportional cluster averaging mirroring `PhylogeneticAnalyzer.BuildUPGMA`; reimplemented in-project because Phylogenetics already references Alignment, so a back-reference would be circular; deterministic lowest-index tie-break); (3) progressive **profile-profile** alignment from the tips using the NW recurrence over columns with sum-of-pairs profile column scoring and the **"once a gap, always a gap"** rule (existing columns copied verbatim; merges only insert whole new all-gap columns). Sources retrieved this session: Feng & Doolittle (1987) J Mol Evol 25:351-360 (PubMed 3118049) — progressive method + guide tree + "Once a gap is introduced … it is preserved within all subsequent fusions"; Wikipedia "Multiple sequence alignment" (guide tree by NJ/UPGMA, sequences added sequentially); Wikipedia UPGMA / Sokal & Michener (1958). **Discriminating star-vs-progressive test:** input `["AAGAA","AACAA","GGTGG","GGTGG"]` (two tight clusters) — progressive yields the correct gap-free length-5 alignment (rows = inputs unchanged, SP −12, all hand-derived), while star inserts a spurious leading gap (length 6, rows `AAG-AA / -AACAA / -GGTGG / -GGTGG`, SP −13); the test asserts the exact gap-free rows + asserts star differs, so it fails against the star aligner. 12 strict tests (null/empty/single/2-seq; identical→no gaps; hand-derived 3-seq `["ACGT","ACGT","AGT"]`→`A-GT` exact columns + SP 8; discriminating two-cluster; invariants equal-length/gap-removal-recovers-input/cols≥max-len/no-all-gap-column; custom scoring; star-unchanged). **Mutation-checked:** inverting the identity distance (wrong guide tree) fails the discriminating test; emitting a non-'-' char for inserted gaps (breaks "once a gap always a gap") fails 3 gap-recovery tests. Full unfiltered suite **6739 green**; build 0 errors (4 pre-existing NUnit2007 warnings only in unrelated `ApproximateMatcher_EditDistance_Tests.cs`; new/changed files warning-free). |
| C5 | RESTR-DIGEST-001 | Circular-molecule digest. | ✅ **IMPLEMENTED** (additive, non-breaking). Added enum `MoleculeTopology { Linear, Circular }` and overload `RestrictionAnalyzer.Digest(DnaSequence, MoleculeTopology, params string[])`; `Linear` delegates to the original `Digest(DnaSequence, params string[])` so existing signatures/outputs are byte-for-byte unchanged. Circular path: distinct forward-strand cut positions normalised mod length, `k` sites → exactly `k` fragments, each running cut→next-cut, the origin-spanning fragment joining last-cut→end with start→first-cut (length `(len − lastCut) + firstCut`); 0 sites → one full-length uncut circular fragment; 1 site → one full-length linearized fragment; on a circle both flanks of every fragment carry an enzyme. Biology re-confirmed this session: Univ. of Illinois MolBio "Restriction Digestion/Gel Electrophoresis" ("If you cut a circle once, you get one linear fragment … cut it a second time to get 2 linear fragments"); Addgene "Plasmids 101: How to Verify Your Plasmid" (single cutter linearizes → 1 fragment; #fragments = #cut sites); Quora summary of the standard rule (linear `k+1` vs circular `k`); EMBOSS `restrict` `-plasmid`/origin-spanning handling. Worked example: EcoRI on 18 bp circle `GAATTCAAAGAATTCAAA` (cuts 1,10) → circular 2 fragments [1,10)="AATTCAAAG"(9) + origin-span [10,18)+[0,1)="AATTCAAAG"(9), sum 18; linear control = 3. Added 5 strict tests (2-site discriminating linear-3-vs-circular-2 + default-overload-equals-linear parity, 0-site, 1-site discriminating linear-2-vs-circular-1, 3-site with origin-span, arg-guards). **Mutation-checked:** forcing the circular path to delegate to linear fails the 3 discriminating count tests. Full unfiltered suite 6716 green; build 0 errors. **Independent re-validation (Phase 3 #2, fresh validator context):** Stage A re-confirmed against externally retrieved sources this session — Univ. of Illinois MolBio (verbatim "If you cut a circle once, you get one linear fragment … cut it a second time to get 2 linear fragments" ⇒ circular `k`→`k`), EMBOSS `restrict` `-plasmid` (sites/cuts "that span the end of the sequence"), Wikipedia "EcoRI" (cut `G↓AATTC`, +1 ⇒ DB `CutPositionForward=1` correct); fragment-count rule (linear `k+1` vs circular `k`) cross-checked. Hand-derived all three implementer examples independently (18 bp 2-site, 12 bp 1-site, 27 bp 3-site) — counts, exact lengths, sequences, and origin-span length `(len−lastCut)+firstCut` all reproduced; no code defect. **Stage-B test-quality hardening (test-only, 0 code change):** the implementer's circular examples are all tandem repeats in which every fragment (incl. the wrap-around) reads "AATTCAAAG", so the origin-span *sequence* assertion is partly self-confirming. Added `Digest_Circular_TwoSites_OriginSpanningSequenceIsUnique_NotTandemRepeat` on a NON-repetitive 18 bp circle `CGAATTCTTTGAATTCAA` (cuts {2,11}): F1 [2,11)="AATTCTTTG"(9), origin-span [11,18)+[0,2)="AATTCAA"+"CG"="AATTCAACG"(9) — a sequence that appears nowhere as a contiguous substring, so it can only form from a correct `tail+head` join; also asserts linear=3 vs circular=2 and sum=18. Mutation-checked: a `head+tail` swap fails this and the 3 discriminating count tests; reverted. Fixture +1; full unfiltered suite **6769 passed, 0 failed**; build 0 errors. Stage A ✅ PASS, Stage B ✅ PASS, ✅ CLEAN. |

| C7 | CRISPR-GUIDE/OFF-001 | Doench/Azimuth on-target, MIT/Hsu off-target weight model. | ✅ **FULLY IMPLEMENTED** (all four published CRISPR scoring models added; no residual). **Implemented (additive, non-breaking — all pre-existing heuristic signatures/tests unchanged):** (1) **On-target — Doench et al. 2014 "Rule Set 1"** (Nat Biotechnol 32:1262, PMID 25184501): added `CrisprDesigner.CalculateOnTargetDoench2014(string context30Mer)` returning 0-100. It is the published logistic linear model over the 30-nt context (4 nt upstream + 20 nt protospacer + 3 nt NGG PAM + 3 nt downstream): `score = intercept(0.59763615) + abs(10−gcCount(seq[4:24]))·gcWeight(gcLow −0.2026259 if gc≤10 else gcHigh −0.1665878) + Σ matched position-specific single/di-nucleotide weights`, then `1/(1+e^−score)`. The 70-entry coefficient table + intercept + GC terms were **transcribed verbatim this session** from the reference implementation `doenchScore.py` in CRISPOR (Haeussler et al. 2016, Genome Biol 17:148; github.com/maximilianh/crisporWebsite). **Cross-check:** an independent Python run of the published coefficients reproduces that file's own two documented worked examples — `TATAGCTGCGATCTGAGGTAGGGAGGGACC` → 0.713089 (×100 = 71.309) and `TCCGCACCTGTCACGGTCGGGGCTTGGCGC` → 0.018984 (×100 = 1.898); the C# impl matches both to <1e-4. (2) **Off-target — MIT/Hsu 2013** (Nat Biotechnol 31:827, PMID 23873081, crispr.mit.edu): added `CalculateMitHitScore(guide20, offTarget20)` (single-hit = `Π over mismatched i of (1−W[i]) × 1/(((19−meanPairwiseDist)/19)·4+1) × 1/nmm² × 100`, special-cased to 100 at 0 mm) and `CalculateMitSpecificityScore(...)` (aggregate = `100/(100+Σ hitScores)·100`), with the published 20-position W vector `[0,0,0.014,0,0,0.395,0.317,0,0.389,0.079,0.445,0.508,0.613,0.851,0.732,0.828,0.615,0.804,0.685,0.583]` transcribed verbatim from CRISPOR `crispor.py` (`calcHitScore`/`calcMitGuideScore`). **Cross-checks (independent Python):** perfect→100; single mm @W[0]→100; @pos5(W=0.395)→60.5; @pos19(W=0.583)→41.7; mm@{5,15}→0.10406·0.345454·0.25·100=0.8987; aggregate one 60.5→62.305; two {60.5,41.7}→49.456. | C8 | PARSE-EMBL-001 | Remote references, deprecated single-dot ranges, dedicated site-between flag. | **IMPLEMENTED** (additive, non-breaking). Extended `EmblParser.Location` with four appended members (`bool IsBetween`, `bool IsSingleBaseFromRange`, `string? RemoteAccession`, `string? RemoteVersion`) plus computed `bool IsRemote`, all defaulting to `false`/`null` so existing local-span output is byte-for-byte unchanged; the shared `SequenceFormatHelper.ParseLocationParts` (used by GenBank) is untouched. `ParseLocation` now (1) strips and captures a remote prefix `accession[.version]:` before parsing the trailing descriptor so accession-version digits no longer leak into the span, (2) parses the site-between operator `n^m` (sets `IsBetween`), and (3) parses the deprecated single-base-from-range `n.m` single-period form (sets `IsSingleBaseFromRange`), distinct from the two-period span `n..m`. Sourced verbatim to INSDC Feature Table Definition §3.4.2.1/§3.4.3 (insdc.org/submitting-standards/feature-table; ftp.ebi.ac.uk/pub/databases/embl/doc/FT_current.txt): `J00194.1:100..202` → bases 100-202 in entry J00194; `123^124` → site between bases 123 and 124; `102.110` → one of bases 102-110 inclusive. Added 12 strict tests (remote ref with/without version, single-base remote, local-not-remote, site-between flag, ordinary-span between=false, single-dot flag, two-dot span flag=false, combined remote+between, malformed remote `J00194.1:`, malformed single-dot `102.`); discriminating vs the old `(\d+)(?:\.\.(\d+))?` regex which captured the `.1` accession digit as a spurious part (Start=1) and mis-parsed `n^m`/`n.m` as two single-base parts with no flag. Mutation-verified (flipping `IsBetween:true`→`false` fails the relevant tests). Existing `ParseLocation_SiteBetween_ParsesRange` unchanged and still green. Full unfiltered suite 6727 green; build 0 errors. |

| ONCO-PHYLO-001 | **No algorithm defect.** `OncologyAnalyzer.ReconstructPhylogeny`/`IdentifyTrunkMutations`/`IdentifyBranchMutations` realise the multi-sample perfect-phylogeny lineage rules verified **verbatim this session** against retrieved primaries: LICHeE (Popic 2015, arxiv.org/pdf/1412.8574, PDF text-extracted) — edge rule **Eq. 2** "(u → v) is added only if … (1) `u.VAFi ≥ v.VAFi − ϵuv` and (2) if `u.VAFi = 0, v.VAFi = 0`" and **Eq. 5** "`Σ_{v:(u→v)∈T} v.VAFi ≤ u.VAFi + ϵ` … the sum of the VAF centroids of all the children must not exceed the centroid of the parent … inequality … does not require all the true lineage branches to have been observed"; PICTograph (Zheng 2022, PMC9344857, WebFetched) — CCF-form sum condition (ε₂=0.2) and lineage precedence/subset-presence (ε₁=0.1). `SatisfiesLineagePrecedence` (`parent < child − ε` ⇒ reject; `parent≤0 & child>0` ⇒ reject) = Eq. 2; `FitsSumRule` via per-node remaining-budget = Eq. 5. Test topologies independently re-derived in Python from the verbatim equations (M2: B↔C both presence-invalid ⇒ forced siblings under A; M3: 0.6+0.6=1.2>1.0 ⇒ sum-rule forces chain) — forced by constraints, not tie-break artifacts. (a) **Structural trunk (BY-DESIGN):** `IdentifyTrunkMutations` = single-child path root→first-branch-point, not strict CCF≈1; consistent with LICHeE's own "trunk branch" (may hold private/partially-shared mutations) and documented in spec/doc. (b) **Default ε=0 (BY-DESIGN):** stricter than source defaults, configurable via `tolerance`. (c) **Deepest-valid-ancestor + id tie-break (BY-DESIGN):** selects one tree among the constraint-valid set; never admits an invalid edge (INV-1/INV-2 always hold). No code/test/spec change required; full unfiltered suite 6677 green; build 0 errors. | Implementation realises Eq. 2 + Eq. 5 exactly; all three notes are sourced/documented design choices, not defects. Tests assert exact sourced parent ids/edges (M1–M3, M8, S2/S3) that a wrong impl (no sum rule, flipped ancestor≥desc) would fail; invariant tests (M6/M7) use the correct inequality form of INV-1/INV-2; full validation matrix with precise exception subtypes. | PANGEN-CORE-001 | **Algorithm defect (fixed).** Core-membership used `coreThreshold = (int)(N·coreFraction)` (floor) with `occupancy ≥ coreThreshold` in both `ConstructPanGenome` and `GetCoreGeneClusters`. Roary's sourced definition (Page et al. 2015, fetched PMC4817141: "a gene being in **at least 99% of samples**") is fractional — `occupancy/N ≥ coreFraction` — **not** floor(coreFraction·N). They diverge for small N: at N=3, coreFraction=0.99 the floor (=2) wrongly classified a 2/3 = 66.7% cluster as core; Roary requires ≥99% (3/3). Fixed with a shared `IsCoreOccupancy(occ,N,cf)` helper (`occ/N ≥ cf − 1e-9`, ε absorbs the 0.99·100 = 98.999… round-off). Fluidity (Kislyuk 2011 PMC3030549, eq. verbatim) and openness (micropan: α<1 open / α>1 closed) were already correct: φ=10/18 hand-derived, M7 α=0→Open and M8 α=1.98→Closed re-derived in Python independently. **Note (PASS-WITH-NOTES):** `DeterminePanGenomeType` fits α by a single dictionary-order log-log regression (order-dependent), not the permutation-averaged micropan nonlinear fit used by the separate `FitHeapsLaw` — disclosed simplification, not a defect. | Test-quality defects fixed in session: S4 was a **green-washed code-echo** locking the wrong floor behaviour ("2/3 is core, CoreGeneCount=2") — rewrote to the sourced fractional rule (CoreGeneCount=1; the 2/3 cluster is accessory), and added S4b locking the exact 99% float boundary (99/100 core, 98/100 not) via `GetCoreGeneClusters`. Description corrected in all three artifacts (algorithm doc, Evidence, TestSpec: INV-03, key-evidence point, S4 row). No assertion weakened; exact sourced values throughout. Fixture 17→18; full suite 6509 green. |

| KMER-DIST-001 | **No algorithm defect.** `KmerAnalyzer.KmerDistance` realises the frequency-variant alignment-free word-composition Euclidean distance verified verbatim this session: the word-vector + union model and the worked example (x=ATGTGTG, y=CATGTG, k=3 ⇒ union {ATG,CAT,GTG,TGT}, c_X=(1,0,2,2), c_Y=(1,1,1,1), "identical ⇒ distance 0") match the **WebFetched** Zielezinski et al. (2017) PMC5627421 Fig. 1; the normalization (count ÷ total k-mers = sum of counts) matches the **WebFetched** Lau et al. (2022) PMC9442500 and the **WebFetched** scikit-bio `kmer_frequencies` reference impl; Euclidean over relative frequencies matches Boden et al. (2014). An independent Python reimplementation reproduced every test value exactly (M1 √0.11=0.33166247903554, M2 0.0, M3 √0.125, M5/S1 √2, S2 1.0, S3 √0.11, C2 0.0, C3 null→1.0/0.0). **BY-DESIGN note (Stage A PASS-WITH-NOTES):** Lau et al. write the divisor as "the total number of k-mers … (i.e. the sequence length minus the k-mer length)" = L − k, an off-by-one in that source's prose; the correct overlapping-window count is **L − k + 1** (WebFetched Wikipedia "K-mer"). The implementation divides by `counts.Values.Sum()` = L − k + 1 (the correct standard), so it does NOT inherit the source's imprecision; this matches the Fig. 1 count vectors and scikit-bio. No code/spec change needed; noted only. | **Test-quality gap fixed in session (no defect):** the three pre-existing permissive tests (tolerance-only identity, `GreaterThan(0)`, `LessThan` ordering) were already removed and replaced by exact-value tests; coverage gap was `null` inputs (documented allowed in the contract, untested). | KMER-STATS-001 | **No algorithm defect.** `KmerAnalyzer.AnalyzeKmers` realises the validated k-mer-spectrum statistics: `TotalKmers = L−k+1 = Σ mult(α)`, `UniqueKmers` = distinct count, Max/Min/Average over the multiplicity table (Average = Total/Distinct), and `Entropy = −Σ p(α) log₂ p(α)` with `p(α)=mult(α)/(L−k+1)`. Sources re-grounded this session: **WebFetched** Wikipedia "K-mer" (L−k+1; GTAGAGCTGT tables k=1 G4/T3/A2/C1, k=2 9 total with GT,AG ×2, k=3 8 distinct; AGAT → AG,GA,AT) and **WebFetched** BioInfoLogics "k-mer counting part I" (ATCGATCAC k=3 → ATC=2 rest=1, 7 total/6 distinct/5 unique; distinct-vs-unique). The **k-entropy** formula was confirmed against the **WebFetched primary** Manca/Bonnici/Franco (2021) arXiv:2106.15351 PDF, verbatim: "E_k(G) = Σ_{α∈D_k(G)} p(α) log₂ p(α) where p(α) = mult_G(α)/(|G|−k+1)". An independent Python reimplementation reproduced every test value exactly: M1 (10,4,4,1,2.5,1.846439344671), M2 (9,7,2,1,1.29,2.725480556998), M3 (8,8,1,1,1.0,3.0), M4 (7,6,2,1,1.17,2.521640636343), M5 (3,3,1,1,1.0,1.584962500721), S1 (3,1,3,3,3.0,0). **BY-DESIGN note (Stage A PASS):** the Manca paper prints the formula *without* the leading minus sign (so E_k as written is ≤0); standard Shannon entropy negates the sum (−Σ p log₂ p) to give a non-negative quantity — the implementation correctly uses the negated form (matching the equipartition-maximum proposition in the same paper that requires H≥0). Sign convention only; no code/spec change. | **No test-quality defect.** The 15-test canonical fixture asserts exact sourced constants within 1e-10 (entropy values M1–M5/S1) and exact integer/record equality for totals, distinct, max, min, and all-zero edge results — a wrong implementation fails the absolute assertion, not an echo. Covers all Stage-A branches: worked examples, homopolymer→entropy 0, all-distinct→log₂D, empty/null→all-zero, k>L→all-zero, k≤0 throws, case-insensitivity. | META-RESIST-001 | **Algorithm defect (fixed).** `BestUngappedMatch` chose the best ungapped alignment by "maximize match count, **tie-break → longer window**". A longer window is reachable only by padding the alignment with **mismatching** flanks, which lowers identity — not how BLAST reports an HSP (Li 2018: identity = matches/columns of the best-scoring segment). Two independent hand-computed counter-examples this session: (1) M3 `contig=TTTCGTA, ref=CGTACGT` — the true alignment is the perfect 4-base HSP `CGTA` (identity 4/4=1.0, coverage 4/7≈0.571, exactly the unit's own Evidence table), but the old code picked offset −1 (window 6, 4 matches → identity **0.667**, coverage 0.857), contradicting the Evidence value (both rejected, but for the wrong reason). (2) **Outcome-changing:** `contig=GGGACGTACG, ref=ACGTACGTAC` (m=10) — true alignment is the perfect 7-base suffix HSP (identity **1.0**, coverage 7/10=0.70 → PASSES default 0.90/0.60), but the old code picked the padded 9-wide window (7 matches → identity **0.778**, coverage 0.90) which FAILS the 0.90 threshold → gene **wrongly missed (false negative)**. **Fix:** tie-break now prefers the **shorter (higher-identity)** window (`matches==bestMatches && bestWindow!=0 && window<bestWindow`); never pads with mismatches. All sourced cross-check values (M1 1.0/1.0, M2 6/7, M3 1.0/0.571, M4 1.0/0.714, M5 0.714, C1 cov-tie, probe 1.0/0.70) re-derived from Li (2018) identity + Zankari (2012) coverage and matched. Doc §4.2 corrected (Stage-A inconsistency N-A2). **Note (PASS-WITH-NOTES, Stage A):** default identity 0.90 is the historical ResFinder **web-service** operating point (corroborated by Sci Rep 2023 / JAC 2016 "90% identity, 60% coverage"); the 2012 paper default is 100% and the ResFinder-4.0 CLI default is 0.80 — sourced, version-specific, explicitly cited. | **Test-quality defect fixed in session:** M3 previously asserted only `Is.Empty` (would pass a wrong implementation; its comment misattributed the rejection to coverage when the old code rejected on identity). Strengthened M3 to expose and lock the sourced identity 1.0 / coverage 4/7 via a lowered coverage floor, and added `FindAntibioticResistanceGenes_EdgePerfectHsp_PreferredOverPaddedWindow` (the outcome-changing probe: perfect 7/10 edge HSP must be REPORTED at default thresholds, identity 1.0 / coverage 0.70 — FAILS old code, PASSES the fix). All MUST/SHOULD/COULD rows covered (identity/coverage paths, both reject branches, best-of-two, identity-tie→coverage, default constants, null×2, threshold-range×2, empty/no-match). No assertion weakened, no skip. Fixture 13→14; full unfiltered suite 6556 green; build 0 errors. |

| CHROM-HOR-001 (no code defect; one test gap closed) | ✅ CLEAN — **No code or description defect.** `ChromosomeAnalyzer.DetectHigherOrderRepeat(string, int monomerLength=171)` → `HorResult` (`ChromosomeAnalyzer.cs:751`), thresholds `InterHorMinIdentityPercent=95.0` (`:728`) / `HorPeriodConsistencyFraction=0.90` (`:734`). **Stage A re-grounded independently this session (WebFetch):** McNulty & Sullivan 2018 (PMC6121732) verbatim — monomer **171 bp**; **intra-HOR monomers 50–70% identical**; **inter-HOR copies "differ by only a few percent"** (~95–100%); "HOR unit length = where the next monomer shows nearly total identity to the first"; HOR units repeated hundreds–thousands of times. Rosandić 2024 (PMC11050224) verbatim — inter-HOR "**less than 5%** divergence" (⇒ ≥95% identity, matching the code's 95.0 constant) and "**period n corresponds to n×171 bp**" (HOR period = k×monomer). The defining identity ordering **inter ≥ intra** is direct (≥95% vs 50–70%). **Independent cross-check (own harness, fixture distinct from repo's; numbers hand-computed):** a **k=4 unit ×m=7 exact copies** array → code reported period **4**, unit length **684 bp** (=4×171), copy number **7** (=⌊28/4⌋), monomer count **28**, mean inter-HOR identity **100.0%**, mean intra-HOR ≈**65%** (hand Hamming 64.91% = (171−60)/171, inside 50–70% band), and **inter ≥ intra** held; a **non-HOR control** (10 mutually-divergent monomers) → `HasHigherOrderStructure=false`, period 1, inter NaN. Custom `monomerLength=10` dimeric unit ×5 → period 2/copy 5/unit 20. All structural quantities match exactly. **Aligner-gap finding (fixture property, NOT a code defect):** intra-HOR identity is a continuous aligner measure; when the background carries short-period autocorrelation the global aligner inserts opportunistic gaps and reports slightly above Hamming. The **repo fixture's** tighter step-2 banded substitutions align **gaplessly** (verified A↔B/A↔C/B↔C = 57.8947% with 0 gaps = exact Hamming), so its hand-derived intra 57.89% and all expected values are correct and **not code echoes**. **Stage A & B PASS.** **No code touched.** **Test-only fix:** prompt edge-case "non-ACGT" was unexercised → added `DetectHigherOrderRepeat_NonAcgtTrailingPartialMonomer_IsIgnored` (3-mer unit ×5 + 80-bp N tail; N tail < 171 bp ⇒ dropped partial monomer ⇒ period 3 / copy 5 / monomers 15 / inter 100% unchanged from M-HOR-1 — hand-derived; behavior pre-verified by the independent harness, incl. that an all-N full monomer drops inter to 91.67% while the 0.90 consistency fraction still detects period 3). Fixture 11→12.
